46: Chapter 40: Continuous wars, plundering from the merchants

46 -40: Continuous wars, plundering from the merchants

Near noon, Gu Wen had just finished breakfast when he heard wailing outside his residence.

Stepping outside, he saw a round-faced merchant with a large belly clutching the legs of a government official and wailing, surrounded by a large group of government officials and government workers continuously moving items out of his house, appearing as if they were about to confiscate everything.

After inquiring through his servants, he learned that the Market Trading Department was collecting taxes again, specifically targeting merchants with a “household tax.”

The Market Trading Department, responsible for the collection of commercial taxes, also managed the taxes for all merchants.

It was led by a deputy director and staffed with eight minor yet influential officials, who tightly controlled the merchants like fearsome beasts.

As for the reason behind their actions resembling a house raid, it was because the tax officers also needed to supplement their household expenses.

Gu Wen tugged at the corner of his mouth, knowing that Daqian was doomed, but things were deteriorating faster than he had anticipated.

At noon, after finishing with the house across the street, the tax officers swarmed toward Gu Wen’s residence.

Gu Wen slowly walked out of his residence, with Qin Mianrong and Rong Leng followed closely by trusted aides wielding swords.

The friction of armor and the heavy footsteps combined, instantly making the ferocious tax collection team seem more approachable.

Particularly Qin Mianrong and Rong Leng, their aura and gazes were not of ordinary imperial guards but of fierce soldiers who had returned from the frontier.

Daqian, even in its lax state, maintained a basic fighting capacity in its frontier troops; otherwise, they would have been overrun by barbarians long ago.

Sometimes, Gu Wen quite admired the frontier troops for managing to hold on for so many years under such a languishing government.

The demeanor of the deputy director of the Market Trading Department had changed from the fierce visage of the morning, and now he greeted with a submissive smile, “Ah, Mr.

Wen, good afternoon.”

“Where’s the peace?

Are you here to confiscate?”

Gu Wen asked indifferently.

There were three steps at the doorway, and he looked down at the official from a higher position.

Since he was here to collect money, his expression was certainly not cheerful.

Yet unaware, a slight emotion triggered the spirit charm, and his dark pupils seemed to contain endless authority, causing the tax officials to feel even more suffocated.

An eight-pound rabbit is a meal for an eagle; an 800-pound rabbit can swallow an eagle.

If you want to kill across species, you need to gain weight; although officials generally have authority over merchants, not every one of them holds high position.

The deputy director of the Market Trading Department was a lowly eighth-ranking officer, but Gu Wen was one of the few major merchants at Dragon Bridge who could not be easily manipulated.

Furthermore, the armored and sword-bearing trusted aides behind Gu Wen were somewhat intimidating.

“Dare not, dare not,” the deputy director of the Market Trading Department replied shamefacedly, stepping forward with a silver piece and whispering, “Mr.

Wen, I’m just following orders.

Please be merciful.”

He even had to bribe me.

Gu Wen found it somewhat amusing, but he would not truly accept it and risk it becoming a handle against him; he pushed the silver back and said, “Sir, just follow the rules, and I will fully cooperate with the government.”

The deputy director immediately sighed in relief and thanked him repeatedly in a low voice.

He wasn’t blind.

Being able to get by in Bianjing required being alert, especially for the executives, because you never know if someone was related to the Emperor.

But the deputy director knew Gu Wen’s identity, a well-known major merchant in Bianjing.

Though not a high-ranking court official, the man was not someone he could afford to offend, especially with imperial guards in his home.

Nevertheless, rules had to be followed, as it was the Emperor demanding the money, and every wealthy household in the city had to pay, including the Chief of Staff.

He took out a document and read:

“Under the sage’s rule, all is tranquil and the people safe in their homes.

Merchants amass wealth unaware of the people’s hardships.

With constant natural disasters and fierce external enemies, the front lines are strained and must be supported by all.

All merchants, great and small, will have taxes increased by thirty percent; any household with more than ten doors and windows will be charged an extra five taels per additional door or window, with no cap.”

Gu Wen’s brows twitched, and even he struggled to maintain his composure at that.

He knew the government was here to collect money and was aware of the government’s monstrous depths, but still felt the urge to curse at this moment.

Taxes on doors and windows, why don’t they just ascend to heaven?

In ancient times, residences, particularly those of the officials and nobles, were well-ventilated and illuminated, usually having many doors and windows, even around the garden walls for decorative purposes.

If evaluated comprehensively, Gu Wen estimated he might need to pay over a thousand taels.

Tax officials entered the residence, each accompanied by a family servant or maid to prevent theft.

This time, the tax officials did not dare act as they had in the morning, plucking hairs on a passing goose, but honestly recorded their findings without taking so much as a needle or thread.

Eventually, the deputy director somewhat sheepishly announced the results: “Marquis Wen, the total is 1,200 taels; I can round it down to 1,000 taels for you if you agree?”

He hoped to offer a face-saving measure to Gu Wen, perhaps fostering future interactions where he could receive favors.

Gu Wen shook his head and said, “No need, sir.

Just conduct official business as usual.”

With a balance of 4,500 taels in his account, deducting 1,200 taels left him with 3,300 taels.

Once all outsiders had left, Gu Wen and Jiang Fugui were in a room where the latter cursed vehemently, not naming names, but everything was self-evident.

At that moment, countless people likely cried out about the unjust heavens, though their curses were not directed at the heavens.

Beyond Qianjing County, numerous eyes were cast towards Bianjing, and within Bianjing, countless citizens looked towards the palace.

Blamed by thousands and bemoaned by many, it was uncertain how much longer this could last.

After drinking a few sips of tea, Gu Wen said calmly, “The ones who should be anxious are not us.”

Throughout history, the rise of dynasties involved myriad bizarre experiences, each unique; however, the scenarios during their downfalls were eerily similar.

When the high and mighty were wasteful, they plundered from the people; with civilian unrest looming, they turned to plundering from the merchants.

Now that they had reached the point of commerce, the next step was to face the relentless rebellion, delegating power locally, causing feudal lords to rise.

The front lines were tense, and the barbarian cavalry that breached the internal defenses couldn’t be ousted.

Should they entrench themselves in Ze County, it would be akin to infiltrating the hinterlands of a former life.

—————–

Ze County.

The smoke of war connected the earth with the sky; peasants pushed the sieging rams that had become mired in mud, while flaming giant rocks soared overhead, crossing one killing field after another, the fires revealing myriad faces of panic, anger, and madness.

Boom!

A giant rock landed on the city wall creating a breach, but it was like a pebble dropped into an ocean wave—swiftly drowned out by innumerable sounds of clashing weapons.

In the deepest part of the largest city of Ze County, Ze City, in a mansion.

The Prefectural Governor of Ze County was bound to a chair, a hand emerged from the darkness, pinching a black bug to insert into his nostril, followed immediately by piercing screams.

The next day, the Prefectural Governor of Ze County defected to the barbarians, and countless noble families defected as well.

Continuous victorious reports from the front lines of Bianjing arrived daily, with officials hastily riding back from outside the city, loudly announcing how many enemies a certain general had destroyed.

It was unclear if it were because of Daqian’s high-quality postal stations that, despite the lengthy journey, they still had the energy to shout loudly.

—————–

Water House.

Gu Wen was reviewing the accounts; last month, the Water House had earned eight thousand silver, deducting a thousand for various costs including wages.

Just yesterday, they had sold a yearly water contract for half-price, amounting to five thousand silver; altogether, that made twelve thousand silver.

He lifted his pen, made a stroke, smooth as running water, and recorded an income of twelve thousand silver!

Standing beside him, Jiang Fugui admired Gu Wen’s admittedly unattractive handwriting, incessantly praising, “Brilliant!

Absolutely brilliant!”

Gu Wen smiled and asked, “What’s brilliant?”

“A golden touch, a ten-thousand-silver stroke, each mark worth ten thousand silver!”

Jiang Fugui also rarely showed literary flair.

The two men exchanged a smile, everything understood without words.

If these merchants only took fixed salaries and dividends, they might not even sustain a lavish lifestyle, much like court officials.

Truly uncorrupt ones could barely ensure their families wouldn’t starve.

Yet Gu Wen and his partner had never been lenient in siphoning revenues from the royal residence; their dictionary lacked the words for “loyalty to the Emperor”.

Two thousand silver in profit; Gu Wen took fifteen hundred, Jiang Fugui got five hundred.

The latter shook his head repeatedly, saying, “Oh no, that won’t do; I hardly contributed.

Just give a hundred as a gesture.

This money doesn’t grow on trees; normal families earn mere ten silver a year.”

Starting from a thousand silver, this was the epitome of living in luxury.

Yet they were only servants to the nobility; the real moneymakers and spenders were always the elite.

With a smile that held an obscure meaning, Gu Wen stated, “Indeed, there are many things I need you to handle.”

“Then, I’ll ask for a reward after the job is done.”

A savings of four thousand five hundred silver, found nineteen hundred, left with five thousand six hundred, under the slogan ‘wealth flowing in continually!’

Nighttime, Dragon Bridge.

No commoners in sight, only distinguished nobility gathered.

A carriage came to a halt, coordinates Mount …

“Mr.

Wen, we’ve arrived.”

Eyes deep and mysterious peered from the shadows, then Gu Wen in his plain black attire, completely according to the court’s regulations for merchant dress, stepped down from the carriage.

Guests and numerous merchants, the beauties from pleasure houses, countless eyes landed on Gu Wen.

At Dragon Bridge, where the elites abounded, rarely could anyone afford armed servants in armor.

Yet Gu Wen received such treatment, a privilege not even Chief of Staffs dared to claim in Bianjing—what immense imperial grace.

Even if only he understood that, beyond protection and prestige, it felt more like a shackle.

The entire scene fell silent, then waiters from various restaurants scurried and competed to invite Gu Wen.

His reputation at Dragon Bridge was sky-high; just a word from him could unite many brothels to crush the market’s corrupt dealers.

Without top-tier elites stepping in, he was truly the undoubted ‘Thousand-Year-Old of Dragon Bridge,’ a title called out by enthusiasts, yet never misnamed.

And the top-tier elites weren’t likely to intervene—the adults wanted it all, both wealth and fame.

Zhao Feng spent hundreds of thousand silvers annually, yet was reputed for his integrity.

Gu Wen entered Qianfeng Tower, since it was business, a record was needed, letting Zhao Feng know he had entered Qianfeng Tower.

Snapping back to reality, a young servant from the brothel called out loudly, “Marquis Wen, honored by your presence at Qianfeng Tower!”

============================================================
Dao Equaling the Heavens
============================================================

47: Chapter 41 One Hundred and Twenty Dragon Tiger Pills

47 -41 One Hundred and Twenty Dragon Tiger Pills

Qianfeng Tower.

As the manager, Yang Shanyu personally welcomed him, unlike last time, this time Gu Wen was more cautious and no longer attributed the agitation he felt in this place to a mere physical reaction.

“Mr.

Wen graces us with his presence, why didn’t you let me know in advance?”

Yang Shanyu was dressed flamboyantly, a half-exposed chest dress suddenly captured the attention of everyone around, countless “old patrons” couldn’t keep their eyes from popping out.

This kind of ‘look but don’t touch’ beauty was most profitable.

Every year countless people came here, even if paying a few dozen Silver Taels to listen to music with the cleansers it was considered worthwhile.

For someone like Yang Shanyu, the appearance fee alone started at a hundred Silver Taels.

Although Gu Wen didn’t think they looked much better than the other girls in Dragon Bridge, people were cheap and liked things on a pedestal.

Gu Wen said, “Gu, just a mere merchant, does not deserve such a grand entrance.”

“Nowadays, who doesn’t know how influential you are, in Bianjing City, the number of people who go out with imperial guards can be counted on one hand.”

Yang Shanyu covered her face and chuckled, then took over from the maid and led Gu Wen up to the third floor; the noise gradually faded to the back, while the bustling sounds of Dragon Bridge still faintly came through.

“Mr.

Wen is here to take over from Hu Sanyuan?”

“Manager Yang really knows how to foresee things.”

“It’s not that I can foresee things, but his death stirred even the Prime Minister.

I figured that since he is dead, the only one who can handle such a big business is Mr.

Wen.”

“I heard about Hu Sanyuan’s death this morning as well, truly a horrific act, dozens of people slaughtered by unknown assailants.”

Gu Wen’s expression remained unchanged, the memories of yesterday’s killing didn’t even make him breathe faster.

Such massacre cases were major incidents throughout the ages, enough to alarm the Prefectural Governor, even to be reported in the imperial court, placed before the Emperor himself.

Bianjing was still under the Emperor’s feet, every issue was significant, only the current Emperor was negligent.

The Prime Minister was already the highest authority, yet what of that.

The greatest fear of murder stemmed from the punishment upon discovery, but the ancient investigative means couldn’t track someone who had traveled twenty miles in two hours and single-handedly annihilated a household.

“Anyone in his line of business would eventually meet their end, the world is full of capable and exceptional people ready to kill them.

If they are displeasing to the eyes, it’s just like stepping on an ant.”

Yang Shanyu said with a concealed smile, her words, if heard by Gu Wen in the past would only make him cleave closer to higher and more prominent officials, but now it was completely different.

She was right, before a cultivator, all were as pigs and dogs.

Even if unable to move mountains and drain seas, as long as the cultivator wasn’t stupid, mortals couldn’t compete.

And I too have embarked on the path of cultivation, and have gone further than anyone else.

—————–

Entering the room, Gu Wen casually sat down while Yang Shanyu served him tea and water.

“This is my first time taking over this matter, can Manager Yang talk to me about it?”

“Of course.”

Yang Shanyu leaned over to pour water, a fragrance assailed the senses, she spoke softly and gently: “Our Qianfeng Tower relies firstly on the cleanliness, and secondly on these nourishing Pills.

I wonder if Mr.

Wen has heard some extraordinary tales.”

Gu Wen responded unmoved, “In these years serving the Ninth Prince, Gu has indeed encountered some.

Otherwise, I wouldn’t be purchasing Dragon Tiger Pills in bulk.

When can I get those Pills I ordered?”

“Dragon Tiger Pills are in high demand, originally Mr.

Wen would have to wait a bit longer for your order.

But since the royal mansion has given us such a large deal, I can make an exception for you.”

Yang Shanyu called for a maid, whispered a few instructions, and soon after the maid left the room, she returned with several wooden boxes.

Delicate redwood boxes padded with satin, each box arranged with twenty Dragon Tiger Pills, a total of six boxes, one hundred and twenty Dragon Tiger Pills.

As previously discussed, seventy Silver Taels a Pill, that would be eight thousand four hundred Silver Taels, yet Gu Wen only had five thousand six hundred silver taels, even adding the two thousand taels deposit at the beginning was not enough.

Even Silver Taels were starting to run short.

Gu Wen sighed, there was nothing he could do, as a merchant, keeping one in ten was already at pinnacles, his ten thousand taels were the limit of not taking risks nor indulging in ill-gotten wealth.

Moreover, his cultivation itself also consumed a lot, Fate Diagram required Heavenly Marrow, ordinary fortune refining Mana also needed medicinal support.

According to Yu Hua, others wanting to quickly recover Mana also needed to ingest Pills.

Money, money, money, everything needed money.

Yang Shanyu said, “This is the most recent batch of Dragon Tiger Pills, how many does Mr.

Wen want?”

“I want it all.”

Without any hesitation, Gu Wen declared his position staunchly.

Though he was penniless, he had Zhao Feng’s silver, and would covet as much as he lacked.

Even if missing a few thousand taels could be noticed, as long as risk could rapidly be converted into power, risk was no longer a risk.

Fist governed the ultimate truth.

The 120 Dragon Tiger Pills equated to twelve years’ worth of Heavenly Marrow, and for a Cultivator with Second Level Five Internal Organs Spirit, each fulfilled organ required two years of Heavenly Marrow, thus totaling ten years for Third Level.

Yang Shanyu was somewhat surprised and asked, “Mr.

Wen, can you really consume so much?”

Gu Wen responded, “Business is always fraught with risks, both the royal court and the business need them.”

“In that case, please pay in full at once, since the amount is rather large.”

Yang Shanyu did not inquire further; as a supplier rather than a storefront like Qianfeng Tower, her focus was solely on selling the goods promptly.

As for how much Gu Wen could profit, that was his own capability.

Gu Wen slapped a stack of treasure papers on the table; spending 6,400 Silver Taels without a hint of heartache, viewing all expenditures as investments in increasing his strength.

Money and cultivation were as dung to gold.

Not to mention, Gu Wen was not footing the bill alone.

Zhao Feng would reimburse half.

With a balance of 5,600 Silver Taels, deducting 6,400 Taels, and with a reimbursement of 3,000 from the royal court, he was left with 2,200 Taels.

Yang Shanyu sent someone to the bank to verify the accounts, as treasure paper was not a currency but more of a paper certificate.

Authenticity required validation through the bank, and possessing treasure paper did not guarantee a direct cash exchange.

Should a ruffian wielding treasure paper enter a bank, they would most likely be invited to dine in prison.

Gu Wen examined a pill, its pale yellow hue speckled with slight black blemishes, indeed different from the crystal-clear top-grade Dragon Tiger Pills.

“There are also the top-grade Dragon Tiger Pills required by the Ninth Prince.”

Another box of pills was presented, containing only five.

Gu Wen quietly sighed, realizing the barriers between circles couldn’t simply be broken through with money.

Without connections, no one would include him, however imposing he might appear in the open streets of Dragon Bridge.

If people had good things, they wouldn’t share them with a mere mortal like him.

“How much?”

“Negotiated by Hu Sanyuan, one top-grade Dragon Tiger Pill costs 1,500 Taels, and we put great effort into improving the success rate.”

“How many low-quality ones does a single batch yield?”

“About fifteen, I suppose.”

“The royal court will cover these low-quality ones as well.

I want the top-grade for 1,000 Taels each, the low-quality for forty each, and don’t want the middle grade.”

Yang Shanyu paused slightly then smiled, “The market price per Dragon Tiger Pill is fifty taels.

You’re not only cutting down 500 Taels but also wanting to purchase the low-quality ones at a discounted rate.

Does Mr.

Wen find that reasonable?”

“Quite reasonable.”

Gu Wen’s gaze was steady, with his right hand resting on his chin, his aura subtly dominated over Yang Shanyu, exuding a mastery over the situation.

This was a rare occasion where he did not need to hide his cunning — he was a merchant, and if he appeared weak in commerce, how could he manage his livelihood?

“The war in Ze State has reached a deadlock lately.

Despite successive victories, each day the troops do not return, peace is not restored.

During such times, major households have the least desire to spend, everyone is tightening their budgets.”

“Your tower’s alchemy is surely not only for selling; keeping these defective products is less useful than selling them to the south through me.

I make money, and you can rapidly reclaim silver.”

He earned money for buying medicine, which was to pursue cultivation.

Similarly, Qianfeng Tower earned money to purchase Spiritual Medicine, selling alchemy products to acquire even more Spiritual Medicine, most of which was undoubtedly consumed internally for cultivation.

One second, two seconds, three seconds…

Yang Shanyu’s smile gradually faded, her expression contemplative, yet she did not agree and said, “Mr.

Wen, please wait a moment, I need to consult with our superior.”

After a short while, she returned and succinctly stated:

“The superior wishes to meet Mr.

Wen.”

This was also beyond expectations.

============================================================
Dao Equaling the Heavens
============================================================

48: Chapter 42 Lu Chan

48 -42 Lu Chan

Qianfeng Tower has six floors; due to architectural limits, the higher the building, the smaller it gets, so by the sixth floor there remains only one room.

Gu Wen entered and was immediately enveloped in a wisp of faint fragrance, while Yang Shanyu stood at the doorway, clearly with no intention of inviting him inside.

Behind the layered curtains in the room, a languid voice emerged from behind the light gauze screens.

“Mr.

Gu is truly a man of great talent.

Your approach to business is always so sharp.

If I didn’t say anything, would you be aware of the profit margins on Dragon Tiger Pills?”

Lu Chan, the Fox Fairy ranked fifth on the Earth List.

“I dare not claim the title of ‘Sir’, nor dare to make reckless comments.”

Gu Wen bowed with hands clasped in front of him, alert in his heart, yet knowing this was an opportunity.

He didn’t need to force his way into the circles of the worldly folk, but if an appropriate chance arose, he didn’t mind securing a niche for himself, convenient for purchasing pills and for acquiring more information so as not to be completely in the dark.

The languid voice spoke again, “Lin Chuan medicinal fruits have a purchase cost of ten taels apiece.

They are the main ingredient needed for concocting Dragon Tiger Pills, requiring five portions, while the numerous auxiliary ingredients are not strict in variety, averaging at five taels each per portion.

Known then, the materials for one portion of Dragon Tiger Pills need fifty-five taels, and on average, fifteen pills are produced per furnace.

How much do we, Qianfeng Tower, earn?”

Is this a math test?

But these pills really are profitable, making over tenfold.

Without hesitation, Gu Wen said, “Subtracting the costs, the total profit is six hundred ninety-five taels.”

“Do you think that’s a lot?”

“Not enough.”

“Then how should we earn more?”

Gu Wen didn’t answer, instead he clasped his hands and said, “That is my trade secret.”

Want to know?

Pay up!

Qianfeng Tower’s hunger marketing is clearly learned from him, but they have only grasped the surface.

Not every product can be sold purely through marketing, nor is marketing suitable for all products.

Dragon Tiger Pills are primarily marketed toward the affluent officials and nobility who frequent brothels, who can be considered as the main consumer group for brothels on Dragon Bridge.

Yet, the inferior Dragon Tiger Pills differ little from ordinary tonic drugs, and ordinary people who consume too much without being able to metabolize it could suffer health issues.

With a small consumer base, weak buying power, and prices that are not exorbitantly high.

In Gu Wen’s view, this was simple logic, but the ancient society couldn’t understand it—not that the people living in that era were stupid, but rather the objective conditions did not allow for it.

In the merchant environment of a feudal dynasty, too much speculation and trickery could easily lead to a crushing blow, and earning too much would leave one devoured by the literati.

The most profitable thing is power, not commerce.

No matter how much Dragon Bridge hustles, they only make a few hundred thousand taels, but salt and iron alone bring in tens of millions per year— their fundamental income from land and grain can no longer be described merely in terms of money.

“Shanyu, take five middle-grade Dragon Tiger Pills to give to Mr.

Gu.”

“Yes.”

As Gu Wen predicted, the other party wouldn’t be stingy with extra payment.

Those only thinking about looting and plundering wouldn’t open a shop on Dragon Bridge, and opening a shop indicated an inclination to cooperate—business itself is a sophisticated social act.

Business is not just about making money but a form of social interaction.

Only groups of a similar nature can come together.

Having obtained the pills, Gu Wen voiced the thoughts he had just harbored, clarifying the benefits and highlighting the flaws in the product.

The other party asked, “So I should raise the price?”

Gu Wen countered with a question, “How long can the Dragon Tiger Pills last?”

Upon receiving the answer that they would lose potency after a month, no wonder Qianfeng Tower did not hoard and consider them as rare commodities.

It turns out they were all short-term goods that couldn’t be stockpiled.

Which means, these items were originally meant to be discarded.

Thus, I can find an opening to seize the profit.

He answered, “In Bianjing, fifty taels each has already created an impression of the product, and since Dragon Tiger Pills can’t be stored, they might as well be sold directly.

If Gu were to sell them to the south, even outside of Daqian.

Bianjing is the most affluent in the whole world, but that doesn’t mean all the world’s wealth is here, and tonic drugs are something all wealthy men need.”

“Selling them outside for five hundred taels each, let the price become the reason to purchase Dragon Tiger Pills, and it can also boost sales in Bianjing.”

Five hundred taels?

Yang Shanyu’s mouth opened slightly in surprise; the price had been multiplied by ten.

Even the room fell silent for a good while.

Gu Wen wasn’t sure what the other party was thinking, but he knew well the ways of pyramid selling—if he said a hundred taels, they would believe it and wouldn’t be moved, but what if it was five hundred taels, or even a thousand?

Moreover, whether the words made sense was not important; what mattered was who spoke them.

“Wealthy merchants in Nanshui number in the millions, and there are countless pelts in Northern Mo; if we can make a name for ourselves, it would be worth more than a thousand taels.”

The other party asked again, “How to sell?”

“If I may be so bold, I can take on the task.”

Gu Wen was ready to show his trump card; with short-term goods, he could greedily exploit to his advantage.

The response was a clear, bell-like laugh, and though the identity of the speaker was elusive, a charming figure already emerged in his mind, even more stunning than Yang Shanyu before him, yet her face remained indistinct.

Misty, unknowable, intangible, yet it leaves one longing for more.

“Mr.

Gu helps the Wang residence with its affairs, could he possibly help me too?”

The jade sword moved, the haze in Gu Wen’s eyes disappeared, but he made no further action, instead repeatedly shaking his head, already having lost the cunning he was known for, thrown off balance.

“The Water House is the Wang residence’s business, and you are the Dragon Tiger Pill’s business—not a conflict.”

Yang Shanyu chuckled to himself: This fellow is also fond of beautiful colors, usually carrying himself like a monk.

“But I’m afraid I may not be able to afford the fee.”

The voice behind the door was soft and melodiously lingering, making one’s bones turn soft upon hearing it.

“Only ten percent is needed, no, even five percent will do—the rest of the fee I will cover.”

“Then I must thank Mr.

Gu~”

—————–

Midnight.

A figure drifted down to Qianfeng Tower, where Yu Hua stood at the entrance, the candlelight casting long shadows, as her leisurely voice drifted out.

“Ah, isn’t this sister Yu Hua?

What wind has blown you to my little sister’s place today?”

The two knew each other but were not close, merely nodding acquaintances.

“Just passing by, decided to come take a look.”

Yu Hua’s tone was even, but in reality, she was not quite at ease, hence the visit.

Fox fairies of the realm, adept in illusion and seduction; their magic seeps through like water with no escape, ensnaring all those with hearts, only varying in severity.

To Yu Hua, the voice was merely pleasant to hear, but the top scholar from Daqian had been thoroughly captivated.

Normally indistinguishable from ordinary people, but the moment Lu Chan spoke, they couldn’t help but want to give their all.

The surrounding noises gradually quieted, sweet sounds enveloping one like multiple hands, caressing and comforting, soothing the hardships within hearts.

Insinuating ever deeper, not saying anything overt, yet feeling like a confidante comforting the soul.

The brilliance of enchantment does not twist the heart but becomes the most wonderful fancy within it.

Why does it sound somewhat like a man’s voice?

“Sister, did you come today to ask the Guardian for medicine?”

“A wastrel who must rely on pills for cultivation—why should I bother?”

Yu Hua’s dao heart remained untouched as she pushed open the door and saw the reflection on the screen; beguiling, full of charm and vitality, sparking imagination.

Stepping further in, past the screen, what met her eyes was not a peerlessly beautiful woman, but a petite, green young girl.

The candlelight elongated her figure; the posture outside the screen was alluring, but inside was the clawing and biting of a young girl.

Fox fairies not only lied but also faked.

It is said that solitary Yin does not thrive; Qianfeng Sect’s cultivation practice side effect is to permanently maintain a youthful appearance, with the higher the cultivation, the younger one appears, until as a baby one becomes a True Monarch.

Foundation Establishment Second Level—not bad.

Lu Chan, seeing the other pass by her set array without any obstacle, had a slightly stiff expression, and her voice lost its aggressive tone, softly asking, “Then what is sister Yu Hua here for today?”

Yu Hua inquired, “I’ve heard that a scholar has written poetry for you recently.”

“Indeed, that’s true.” Lu Chan’s eyes gleamed and, as Yu Hua predicted, she proudly recited, “A smile alone blooms a hundred flowers, a glance brings radiance and divine vigor.

Though it describes me, it should also be fitting for Sister Yu Hua.”

She knew of Yu Hua’s taste; despite never taking the spotlight, others rarely offered her poems, always watching silently from the sidelines.

Perhaps out of disdain, but is there anyone without admiration?

Not needing doesn’t mean not liking.

What responded to her was a clear and refined voice.

“Clouds wish for attire, flowers yearn for beauty, spring breeze brushes the threshold, dew laden with fragrance.

Unless on the summit of a sea of jades, one would only meet her under the moon at the Jade Terrace.”

Lu Chan’s eyes widened slightly, then gradually darkened.

More than just being upstaged—utterly embarrassed.

Yet Yu Hua smiled.

She tilted her head and asked, “How did you know someone wrote poetry for me?”

Having said her piece, she turned and left, her spirit clear and refreshed.

Lu Chan hastily followed, inquiring, “May I ask sister, who wrote this poem?”

Yu Hua didn’t reply but simply glanced back, causing the other to feel like facing a great enemy, daring not to err again.

Not until her figure disappeared into the vast night did Lu Chan purse her red lips; just now, she had felt a hint of killing intent emanating from the other.

Such a big reaction just for a name, who could it be?

Gossip curiosity stirred within her, yet without a clue to pursue.

Dao Equaling the Heavens
============================================================

49: Chapter 43: With vehement conviction, a clear intent to vanquish

49 -43: With vehement conviction, a clear intent to vanquish

Gu Wen regained his composure and found himself on the first floor.

He didn’t return to his mansion; instead, he chose to stay overnight at Qianfeng Tower.

Because he feared being robbed on the way back, not that being robbed was the main concern, but exposing his true strength was.

Yang Shanyu escorted him back to his room and said, “Mr.

Wen, you should rest early.”

“When will the pill His Highness requested be ready?”

“Three days from now.”

The door closed, and Gu Wen lay on his bed.

The shadowy figure that fluttered like a wind chime still echoed in his mind.

He circulated the Yuqing Sword Skill, and the jade sword trembled slightly.

All distracting thoughts were scattered wherever the heart sword passed.

When he opened his eyes again, his gaze held a hint of wariness.

Indeed, the reputation of the fifth on the Earth List was well-deserved.

Even with preparation, he had still been affected.

He hadn’t lost his mind just now; he was clear about what he was doing and could control his actions.

But the runaway thoughts behind the door couldn’t be contained, and if this continued without resistance, he’d eventually succumb.

And his original plan to buy Dragon Tiger Pills at a reduced price had fallen through, and instead, he ended up working for free to help them—it was like sponging off the sect.

Gu Wen chuckled to himself: ‘Speculating on futures often leads to losses; every business has its risks.’

Coincidentally, I also want to sponge.

—————–

The next day, Gu Wen first went to the royal palace to deliver the pill.

Because of the need for secrecy, he couldn’t just turn up at the Qianfeng Tower and then head straight to the palace.

He found it amusingly similar to the feeling of going to an internet cafe in his past life, just as parents couldn’t stand guard at the entrance of an internet cafe, the imperial palace also couldn’t know everything.

The court lacked a special intelligence agency like the Jinyi Guard and was long accustomed to a ‘monarch-offline’ system.

But the imperial palace must have known about Qianfeng Tower selling pills.

For a merchant like him to stay overnight at a brothel was normal, but coming and going would be suspicious.

This was for secrecy and also to protect his own pills.

“With Mr.

Gu here, it is indeed a blessing for this prince.”

Zhao Feng was very pleased and verbally commended Gu Wen, but offered no tangible rewards,

After all, he was out of money, having almost emptied his reserves to buy the Condensing Dao Pill.

This wasn’t just a matter of money, but also of the many treasures he had accumulated over the years.

Gu Wen clasped his hands and said, “It is my honor to alleviate Your Highness’s worries.”

Seeing him so loyal and devoted, Zhao Feng’s usually negligible conscience flickered slightly, and he added, “Mr.

Gu, do you wish for the longevity of immortal cultivation?”

Gu Wen was somewhat surprised.

Could it be that this fellow had been possessed?

He feigned delight and nodded eagerly: “Naturally, I do desire it.

Although I am but a commoner in plain clothing, I too wish to live longer.”

“To cultivate the Dao, to become an Immortal, to seek eternal life— throughout history, how many kings, nobles, and generals have longed for longevity.

What they could not obtain, I can offer you.”

Zhao Feng repeated these words with a pale face and eyes brimming with spirit light resembling a Divine being, though to Gu Wen, he seemed no more significant than an ant.

What was certain, however, was that Zhao Feng had finally embarked on cultivation, his eyes reflecting additional spirit light.

Gu Wen couldn’t tell if Zhao Feng was just weak or if it was the aftermath of taking pills, but the foundation of the Dao was inherently natural.

Gu Wen could perfectly conceal his aura, while Zhao Feng leaked like a sieve.

Zhao Feng boasted proudly to him, “But whether you succeed will entirely depend on your performance.”

It was merely my overthinking.

“Thank you, Your Highness.

To undergo fires and tread through waters for you is my unhesitant duty.”

“Good.”

Gu Wen, with his head bowed, added, “Your Highness, regarding the pill…”

“You need only bring it to me.”

Zhao Feng interrupted, his tone forceful but revealing his panic, like a student trying to cheat for good grades.

Gu Wen wasn’t intimidated and continued to ask, “I encountered the proprietor of Qianfeng Tower, and she mentioned that the pill’s toxicity is unpredictable and varied from person to person.

Have you noticed anything unusual lately?”

“This…”

Zhao Feng hesitated for a moment, then considering Gu Wen was just a mortal and a servant at that, he said, “I’ve experienced qi and blood deficiency lately, often coughing, and I have to take Dragon Tiger Pills for my cultivation, otherwise my chest feels hot.”

—————–

Another day passed, and there was one day left until the Condensing Dao Pill was ready.

After establishing a connection, meeting with Lu Chan became much simpler.

She probably thought that she had successfully planted a spy within the royal house.

After explaining Zhao Feng’s condition to her, Gu Wen asked, “The prince’s cultivation is increasingly difficult.

Might he pause for a while?”

Lu Chan replied, “Building one’s foundation is like going against the heavens.

Once you start, retreating is like severing one’s own arm.

I will give him the Condensing Dao Pill, whether he continues or not is up to him.”

“Yes.”

As Gu Wen was about to leave, clasping his hands, Lu Chan suddenly stopped him and asked, “Do you know if Yu Hua, apart from Zhao Feng, has been in contact with anyone else?”

“I have only seen Yu Hua, the immortal, and do not know whom else she has met.”

“Truly useless.”

Lu Chan’s voice took on a note of displeasure, but upon seeing Gu Wen’s demeanor, she let it go.

It would be odd for a mere mortal to have access to Yu Hua, as that Daoist woman was very proud, even more so after entering Daqian.

Her voice shifted and she leaned in to ask Gu Wen, “Please help me inquire about this, Mr.

Gu.”

This damn hypocrite.

Gu Wen thought bitterly if he saw her true face, he might still call out ‘little demon’.

For now, lying in wait, he bowed and said, “I would be honored to serve the immortal.”

Gu Wen boarded his carriage to leave.

Through the curtained carriage window, he sensed two gazes upon him and lifted a corner to peek.

One was from a monk with a face covered in flesh, the other from Hee Huan, a handsome man in white.

They looked at him as if they saw a harmless rabbit, a mundane and harmless commoner.

Come then, the more the merrier.

There were ten hours left until the Condensing Dao Pill was ready.

—————–

Water House.

Gu Wen adjusted the ledger again, concealing the silver he used for reimbursement and striking the corresponding water bills—commonly known as fraudulent accounting.

The royal palace wouldn’t notice until next year, and by then, it was uncertain whether he’d even still be in Bianjing.

Dao Equaling the Heavens

50: Chapter 43: His Intense Purpose, Clearly a Resolve to Kill and Conquer_2

50 -43: His Intense Purpose, Clearly a Resolve to Kill and Conquer_2

“Master, I’ve found the bed beam wood you wanted.”

The voice of Jiang Fugui came through, followed by a root wrapped in black cloth extending from the doorway.

Then, Jiang Fugui entered the room, cautiously adjusting its angle before placing it on the ground.

He slightly unraveled one end of the black cloth.

A hint of cold light twinkled, and the spearhead reflected lightly.

Jiang Fugui smiled and said, “Master, the top-quality bed beam wood you requested!”

In Bianjing, armor is the primary prohibition, crossbows are second, and knives, spears, swords, and halberds are third.

The first two are only stored in the armory; ordinary imperial guards wouldn’t necessarily have them.

Armor wore only started to be permitted by the court in response to frequent civil unrest in the last two years.

While knives, spears, swords, and halberds were also banned, supervision was lax, and they could still be obtained.

Gu Wen weighed it in his hand, one zhang long and weighing three jin.

It had an ancient version of a composite material, tendon wood for the pole, and the spearhead had a curved blade, with crescent-shaped side blades that made it easy to stab and pull out.

It was somewhat similar to a crow-head spear.

Holding it wasn’t strenuous; he instead felt it was too light, reminiscent of a monkey selecting weapons at the Dragon Palace of the East Sea.

A weapon one jin heavy, the hand wielding ten jin of force.

But holding a hundred jin of force while the weapon only weighed one jin felt slightly awkward, but he would make do with it for now.

“Where did you get this from?”

“The tooth market.

Reportedly, it belonged to a destitute descendant of a general who sold it.

I spent a hundred taels.”

“Very good.

Come sit with me at this time tomorrow to provide cover for me, making people believe I haven’t left.”

“Understood, master.”

Jiang Fugui had learned the essence of Gu Wen, never asking questions that shouldn’t be asked.

There were still nine two-hour periods before the Condensing Dao Pill was ready.

Gu Wen looked at the completely dark sky outside and made a firm decision inwardly.

He wrote “200,000” in the ledger.

This was the amount he had disbursed from the royal residence and the sum he had spent bribing the royal storeroom keeper to tally the inventory.

Ultimately, this was what the royal house had spent in the past half-month.

Practically cleansing Zhao Feng’s entire fortune.

An hour later, Gu Wen met with Hee Huan in disguise.

He cut to the chase and said, “When the pill is ready, you and I will directly storm into Qianfeng Tower.”

Hee Huan shook his head, “Such a move will put us at odds with the Fox Fairy.

It’s better to wait for the merchant to bring out the item.”

“No, I want to be at odds with her.

I’m very curious to see what she’s truly capable of.”

A fighting spirit flared in the only visible part of his eyes under the hooded cloak, causing Hee Huan a headache.

Despite his efforts to persuade, he couldn’t sway the martial fanatic before him.

Reluctantly shrugging, he said, “If Fellow Daoist Red Dust insists on being so reckless, then I cannot accompany you.”

“You don’t need to come in with me, just back me up from outside.

If things go south, you run.”

“Fellow Daoist is truly noble!”

Hee Huan quickly changed his words.

They agreed that at sunset, they would forcibly seize the pill.

—————–

Back at home, Gu Wen locked the doors and windows and looked at the 120 Dragon Tiger Pills on the table, his eyes nearly curved into smiles.

Today he was not poor; he was a Dao Master!

For safety, he first took ten pills to try.

They tasted fishy and spicy, as if fire roasting within his stomach.

His Fate Diagram vibrated, meteors of fire danced in the sky, and the Heavenly Marrow Fire kept increasing.

[Heavenly Marrow, two years]

Gu Wen opened his eyes and glanced at his body, which reacted greatly.

But with the Yuqing Daoji cultivation protecting his mind, his thoughts weren’t uncontrollable.

In meditation, he channeled the chaotic properties of the medicine as hot currents into his Qi Sea, slowly transforming them into Mana.

Continuing this process from daytime into nighttime, the 120 Dragon Tiger Pills were quickly consumed.

Adding the Qi Nourishing Pills given by Yu Hua earlier…

[Heavenly Marrow, thirteen years]

Eleven years of Heavenly Marrow could improve the Dao Foundation further, breaking through two levels of the Yuqing Sword Skill, continuously innovating the Xuanming Spear, and strengthening the Spiritual Jade Body Protection Skill, making the Moonset Step faster and more distant.

He could invest in expanding the Dao Foundation to reach greater future heights, or expect deeper understanding from the Yuqing Sword Skill that could turn breath into sword.

Alternatively, directly enhance strength with the Xuanming Spear or focus on defense and speed.

The Dao Master was richer than ever before, with wealth beyond spending, truly unspendable.

This smooth-sailing future had Gu Wen utterly fascinated.

People like Zhao Feng, born into nobility and leading smooth, successful lives, could never understand.

Only those stuck in the mire cherish every slight chance for ascent.

Gu Wen channeled energy to calm his emotions, then gazed thoughtfully at the various Cultivation Techniques before him.

Deciding between the Yuqing Heart Method dictating limits and Mana, the highly effective combat Xuanming Spear, the defensive Spiritual Jade Body Protection Skill, the escape and pursuit capable Moonset Step, and the Yuqing Sword Skill which seemed trivial but could surprise opponents.

All five cultivation techniques were bestowed by Yu Hua, carefully chosen for significant personal enhancement.

Long-term, the Yuqing Dao Foundation was certainly the best choice, but lacking sufficient Qi nourishing pills and having never fully filled his Dantian Qi Sea, what should he do if investing ten Heavenly Marrows did not significantly enhance the Third Level?

He had witnessed the marvel of the Dao Foundation but also realized a problem: however much the limit is expanded, reserves are needed.

Most crucially, there were two days until the raid to snatch the Condensing Dao Pill.

Should he pursue stability, profit, or both?

Naturally, he would opt for completeness!

Five years ago, at the moment he kneeled before Zhao Feng, he had said to himself.

“Endure in obscurity until death, or rise with the wind.

You’ve sung for so long.

Now it’s my turn to take the stage.”

Submerging into the Qi Sea, looking up at the Fate Diagram resembling the universe, abundant meteors of fire spiraled and swirled, covering the dome of the sky with fire.

The universe trembled as the meteors fell.

Lacking offensive weapons, he refined an unparalleled Gang Qi.

Dao Equaling the Heavens

51: Chapter 43: His Intense Purpose, Clearly a Resolve to Kill and Conquer_3

51 -43: His Intense Purpose, Clearly a Resolve to Kill and Conquer_3

[Xuanming Spear, Fifth Level, Xuanming Spear Intent]

In the art of war, above the art lies the Gang Qi, then comes the intent, and above all, the Divine, all fulfilled by returning to the art.

Having refined the Xuanming Spear with Heavenly Marrow for two years, it was expected that four years of Heavenly Marrow could refine the Spear Intent.

However, Gu Wen, through the understanding of Sword Intent, found a way and succeeded.

Advancing further would be from Spear Intent to Divine, which would require eight years of Heavenly Marrow.

Heavenly Marrow flowed abundantly, with eight years of Heavenly Marrow turning into a stone mill, grinding open the narrow path of the Xuanming Spear.

The Xuanming Spear had no Fourth Level, let alone a Sixth Level Spear Divine.

Gu Wen carried the spear, walking step by step along the path defined by Heavenly Marrow, knowing that by following the Spear Intent of Heavenly Marrow, one could reach a level of spear mastery sufficient to ascend the Immortal Land’s rankings.

Yu Hua once said, “The rankings of men judge strength, with the victor crowned king.

The rankings of the land judge talent, with the most talented at the top.”

Beyond the heavens, where the stone tablets of Immortal Land were vast, an old man with white hair and squinted eyes was polishing the inscriptions.

Suddenly, a streak of golden light appeared, and a new name emerged.

[Immortal Land Rankings, number 81, Red Dust, Xuanming Spear Divine]

The old man’s polishing movements remained unchanged, while the Divine Thoughts cast from the surroundings flickered and vanished.

The name Red Dust was noted by some, but merely noted.

The Immortal Land Rankings, like the Human Rankings, forecast future achievements, whereas the latter represents present strength.

To be ranked among them all is to be a heavenly prodigy, still, the rank of eighty-one somewhat falls short.

One year of Heavenly Marrow.

Three years of Heavenly Marrow.

Five years of Heavenly Marrow.

Seven years of Heavenly Marrow.

Gu Wen stopped, the flow of Heavenly Marrow ceased, and one step ahead was a dark spear.

Its rhythm was bold and sweeping, filled with an unstoppable will.

The Xuanming Spear was originally created by a martial artist in the Qi Cultivation Stage, and though refined to the ultimate, it remained a Qi Cultivation technique, his aspirations no more than defeating the enemy before him.

A stride is six feet, mastery in a square inch.

For this step, why require Heavenly Marrow?

With a single step forward, Gu Wen reached out and grasped the dark spear, the Heavenly Marrow unspent, his spear technique divine.

“Why would I need this six-foot spear of a martial artist?”

A wild smile cracked his lips, his eyes brimming with disdain, as if he looked down upon all beings, considering them all inferior.

“My ambition should be to cleanse the entire world, leaving not a speck of dirt under the heavens!”

He released the dark spear and turned to walk in another direction, continuing through eight, nine, ten, eleven, twelve years of Heavenly Marrow!

The dark red Gang Qi burned like a fierce fire, and a murderous aura surged skyward.

With one step, he trod the path of slaughter, with one punch, avenged blood spilled.

In a hazy realm, with every step countless broken spears lay about, and where his gaze fell, mountains of corpses and seas of blood.

Gu Wen looked up to see a crimson streak then across the sky, scales and splendor tumbling, clouds compressed, and massive pupils leisurely opened, ultimately fixing upon a red dragon.

The Spear Intent was like a dragon, the murderous aura as deep as an abyss.

The red dragon bowed its head, and Gu Wen caressed its Dragon Head, his eyelids drooping softly, an unprecedented tenderness in his smile, yet an endless murderous intent arose.

“Let’s call you the Flame Spear, with intent as fierce as the flame, as clear as the act of slaughter.”

Fierce, to annihilate all under the heavens, to erase all impurities.

Flame, upright and just, luminous as the day.

If I am benevolent, the world is not.

Beyond the heavens, the stone tablet of Immortal Land shook, the old man polishing the inscriptions slightly opened his eyes, only to see the word Red Dust trembling, strands of red light bursting forth.

With a triumphant song, he stepped forward, one step at a time, trampling down numerous talents from the Major Sects.

[Immortal Land Rankings, number 6, Lu Chan, Fox Fairy of illusion, where the illusion becomes reality, and reality becomes illusion.]

[Immortal Land Rankings, number 5, Red Dust, Spear of Slaughter, with fierce intent, clear as the act of killing.]

Three days ago, a prodigy without sect or lineage crashed into the top ten of the Human Rankings.

Three days later, he ascended to number five of the Immortal Land Rankings.

Numerous Divine Thoughts hurried back, shocked, then silent.

No one knew who the person with the dao name Red Dust was, regardless of how they calculated fortunes, they could not glimpse a thread of his destiny.

Yet, the name Red Dust had entered the eyes of all the great powers between heaven and earth.

This was the first real opening of the Immortal Land, and it would also be the last.

This era, where prodigies gathered, the Divine reincarnated, and saints entered the game.

Talent is merely the qualification to enter, invincibility just the preparation to take the stage, only the Immortals are the play’s actors.

And Gu Wen, a commoner and a house servant, half a year into his cultivation, what he sought was to take the stage and act.

To perform the first of the distinguished men, the summit of the earthly talents.

============================================================
Dao Equaling the Heavens
============================================================

52: Chapter 44 Flame Spear

52 -44 Flame Spear

Early morning, sunlight streamed in through the window.

Gu Wen slowly exhaled a breath of dull energy, which transformed into Gang Qi and left holes upon touching the ground.

He opened his eyes, a trace of killing intent in his gaze that could not be dismissed, nor was it a surge of emotional tumult but rather the calm, profound depths of an abyss.

[Flame Spear, evolved from the Xuanming Spear, perfecting the art of moves, exhausting the murderous intents of heaven and earth.]

[First Level, Ming Jin, where force and energy fuse into one, unmatched in ferocity.]

[Second Level, An Jin, hidden within the form, invisible from the outside, moving like thunder.]

[Third Level, Xuan Jin, turning the tangible into intangible, merging myriad forces into one.]

The first three levels were still based on the Xuanming Spear, a cultivation technique during the Qi Cultivation Stage without any flaws, even considered reaching the pinnacle.

A warrior’s ultimate exploration of mortal martial arts, the human body’s ultimate use of polearms, where countless moves adhere to a central principle.

But the next three levels were where Gu Wen truly exceeded beyond the original.

[Fourth Level, Flame Spear Gang, enveloped by Gang Qi, shocks ten thousand troops, hard as iron.]

[Fifth Level, Flame Spear Intent, the spear technique penetrates the mysterious, Intent moves with the spear, demolishing the solid and eradicating the spirit.]

The Fourth Level transformed into a new form of Gang, its power and added hardness was twice that of the Xuanming Spear, while the consumption of Mana only increased slightly.

The Fifth Level underwent the greatest change, incorporating a trace of Divine Soul attack, with the spear’s Intent, the enemy would become dazed, even stiffened with fright.

For instance, using the spear’s Intent to freeze someone with a glance.

At last…

Gu Wen right hand loosely gripped, a streak of dark red fire spread, and a dark red spear materialized in his hand, ten feet long, weightless, radiating a fierce blood light, emitting only killing intent as cold as ice upon contact.

A plain, unadorned Daoist Soldier.

[Sixth Level, Flame Spear God, spear technique merges with the divine, mimics heaven and earth, the art of the dharma form.]

Yu Hua had said, above the Daoist Soldier’s art of war were the Gang, then the Intent, and above them was the God, fulfilled by the law.

Often, those who mastered the divine realm of martial arts were among the strongest just below the True Monarchs, their combat strength far surpassing that of other cultivators.

That was his greatest gain, and the most dominant martial power Gu Wen had ever mastered!

With a thought, Gu Wen resonated with the Flame Spear, the deeply mystical sense turned into the plainest and most unadorned meaning within his cognition.

Invincible within a square inch, lifelessness within six feet.

Killing and drinking blood, nurturing the Daoist Soldier.

Close-quarters unmatched, the energy from killing could nurture the weapon.

Gu Wen felt an unprecedented ease of mind and body, this sensation of controlling power addicted him.

After half a year of cultivation, he had the strength of a thousand catties in his hands, his breath could form Gang Qi, and he could kill with a nod.

Though he could not topple cities or shatter mountains, strength was relative.

If there were not the great powers moving mountains and seas, then Gu Wen was undoubtedly among the very top of Daqian, at least within the top ten.

But with this cultivation, what about facing an army?

On the plains, he had no chance against cavalry, facing the coordinated volleys of powerful crossbows was a matter of life and death, and getting trapped in a military formation meant certain death.

This was Gu Wen’s assessment.

Aside from these three circumstances, his death was almost impossible.

And this wasn’t a flaw in cultivation, it was a change brought about by cultivation.

Ordinary people facing an army couldn’t even resist regular infantrymen wielding knives, let alone cavalry or heavy-armored infantry.

On Jianghu, martial arts experts have to kneel before even the most ordinary infantry.

Cultivation made it so that the army posed a threat only under strict conditions, conditions the army itself could hardly create proactively; only if he went mad and handed the enemy a knife could such a situation possibly arise.

Armies on the move often numbered thousands, or even tens of thousands, the long treks requiring logistical support many times that of the regular forces.

Even trapped within the city of Bianjing, Gu Wen was confident he could escape, as long as he didn’t brazenly storm through the city gates.

Relying on the complex terrain within the city, he could overpower five or six people, military formations of dozens could not deploy properly, and hundreds would only disrupt their own ranks.

Gu Wen felt certain and his mood lifted as never before, living cautiously and discreetly for five years just like a monkey pressed under the Five Elements Mountain, today he finally managed to stretch himself a bit.

He turned his head again towards the window, the imperial aura passed over from the direction of the palace.

The real danger was the Lord Emperor.

Although it seemed Yu Hua might be able to suppress the other, he ultimately did not like to rely on someone else for hope.

He closed his eyes, nurtured his energy, the Qi Sea in his dantian had grown to the size of a basketball.

Without Qi Nourishing Pills there could be no rapid growth, but whatever little could be gathered was still something.

Thud, thud, thud.

The room door was knocked, and the voice of the little eunuch came through.

“Mr.

Wen, are you awake?”

Gu Wen got out of bed to open the door and meet the visitor, the little eunuch Feng Baoming conveyed a message, “Mr.

Wen, His Highness wants you to deliver the Water House’s account books to the prince’s mansion by 7 p.m.”

“I understand.”

The little eunuch left; he was unaware of the matter concerning the Pills, serving just as a messenger.

It seemed that Zhao Feng was indeed in a hurry.

Gu Wen was not, however.

He returned to his room to meditate again, his mind sinking into the Qi Sea.

[Heavenly Marrow for one year]

Heavenly fire smelts; sagacity turns into broth.

A round of moonlight appeared on the Qi Sea, a figure floated in the air, now leaping thirty feet high, now gliding a hundred meters, akin to the light kung fu one reads about in martial arts novels from a previous life.

Light kung fu existed in this world, but it required immortal cultivation.

[Moonset Step, Second Level: Short leap like the wind, light as a swallow]

It allowed him to move extremely fast over short distances, dodging moves as if propelled, achieving effects similar to teleportation; the downside being it consumed five times more energy than the First Level.

The final level of Moonset Step, the Third Level Ling Yue, made the practitioner light as a feather, leaping thirty feet in one bound.

[Heavenly Marrow depleted]

“Second Level is enough for now.”

—————–

At noon, Water House.

Gu Wen went to the Water House to eat; the meat, eggs, and dairy on the table changed with the season.

Gu Wen liked lamb, but due to Daqian waging war with the barbarians in the north, the price of lamb was high, so it had been replaced with chicken.

Little Fullness bitter herbs, which clear heat and relieve fire, also made it to the table.

Jiang Fugui brought his teenage son, Jiang Jucai, to familiarize him with Gu Wen, establishing a sort of nepotistic relationship.

Unlike his father who had a sneaky appearance, Jiang Jucai had a noble countenance and exuded the aura of a scholar after years of study.

Their family belonged to the classic model where the grandfather trades, the son studies, and the grandson enters the bureaucracy, potentially stepping into the gentry class after three generations of effort.

Gu Wen was not overly interested in these ‘grand endeavors,’ but that didn’t stop Jiang Fugui from incessantly talking about studying, civil examinations, and entering officialdom.

“Has the silk sent from South Water County via the river arrived?”

Gu Wen remembered the matter of the silk.

Jiang Fugui replied, “It has arrived, but the handcraft industry in South Water County is thriving, all processed into threads and even fabrics.

They brought it here to earn extra processing fees.

It may be a bit tough for us to handle it profitably, as there is neither money nor fame in it.”

The profit margins for fabric were always low; otherwise, Jiang Fugui, used to doing business at Dragon Bridge, would not have considered it.

“The people of Bianjing need to eat in these depressive times; I must work even if the earnings are lesser.”

Gu Wen spoke as calmly as usual, yet his actions were drastically different.

“Good business lies in real deeds that rescue the people.”

The textile mills had always been the backbone of the city’s industry; apart from agriculture, they employed the most people and were closely connected to everyone.

Thus, the imperial government strictly regulated them with numerous taxes, generally a tough business without gratification.

Most of the mills were therefore operated by the government.

Jiang Fugui was stunned for a moment, sensing something different about Mr.

Wen, yet unable to articulate it.

In the past, Mr.

Wen also helped the impoverished, but the only difference was he never directly stated his intentions to help the people; he disliked fame and resisted being well-known.

Today, however, there was an extra touch of righteousness to him and an undeniable majesty hard to conceal.

One more hour until the Pills were ready.

Gu Wen instructed Jiang Fugui to guard the outside, letting no one in, and Jiang Fugui, as always, asked no questions.

He donned his night attire, covered his face with a hat, and climbed out the window.

Outside, the setting sun made his black-clad, masked figure particularly conspicuous, but the purpose of the outfit was not to make him unseen but unrecognizable.

Thus, he could freely indulge as he wished.

============================================================
Dao Equaling the Heavens
============================================================

53: Chapter 45 Horse Treads on Dragon Bridge

53 -45 Horse Treads on Dragon Bridge

Dragon Bridge Night Market.

Hee Huan leaned against the wall of a small alley, accompanied by a gaunt woman, the two flirting with each other, deeply enamored.

Suddenly, a dark shadow descended and Gu Wen stood in front of them, his towering figure casting them into shade, his eyes under the bamboo hat glowing red with a faint ghostly light.

It wasn’t just any mortal woman who would have been frightened; even Hee Huan himself was taken aback, not understanding why the sense of oppression emanating from this man had intensified so much more than before.

He covered the woman’s mouth and comforted her as before, “Don’t be scared, my dear.

This man is a friend of mine.”

My dear?

Gu Wen looked at the somewhat familiar face in front of him.

Wasn’t this the woman he had encountered in the tooth market before Yu Hua descended to the mortal realm?

He remembered that she had been so unattractive that she struggled to even sell herself, and now she had become this fellow’s wife?

Seeming to understand his confusion, Hee Huan explained, “Fellow Red Dust, this is my third wife named Cui Lan from Daqian.

I came across her selling herself when I first entered the mortal world.

Seeing her without parents and disliked for her looks, I took her into my household.”

“Cui Lan, you go home first and prepare dinner with the others; I’ll be back.”

“Yes, husband.”

The scar-faced woman left.

Gu Wen’s expression was odd as he oddly praised, “You’re quite a philanthropist, Fellow Daoist.”

Previously, he had disregarded the beauties from prestigious families, instead choosing a homeless woman off the street.

Moral values change with the times, and good and evil are seen relative to the situation.

Hee Huan, appearing to be a womanizer, was in some sense also a rescuer, albeit with somewhat bizarre methods.

Hearing the praise, Hee Huan paused momentarily, then he stepped forward, gripping Gu Wen’s shoulder as if he had found a bosom friend.

“Fellow Red Dust understands me!

The outside world spreads rumors of my licentious nature, with over a hundred wives and concubines, yet they don’t know that I never disturb honorable families.

Most of my wives are unfortunate souls; I simply want to give them a home!”

“So you mean to say you’re doing all this to save people?”

“I’m just lascivious.”

Hee Huan spoke seriously and honestly.

He, in a way, explained to Gu Wen as if he were promoting a product: “Our sect practices Dual Cultivation, and although it’s not the Cauldron method, it does require the union of Yin and Yang.

Therefore, it’s common to see multiple husbands or wives, as well as mutual cultivator relationships.

However, my taste is much higher than that of the sect and even the entire world.

Don’t you think it’s beautiful that a lonely damsel sees you as her only one?”

“Such deep love, such intense affection, that is what those lofty female cultivators lack.

What I seek is the utmost in sentiment!”

Gu Wen brushed off his hand, failing to grasp his way of thinking, “With so many people, aren’t you afraid they’ll cheat?”

“If that happens, then it simply means my own strength is inadequate, though it has never happened to me thus far.

As for matters of the chamber, it is fundamentally my cultivation.”

“….”

Gu Wen could only inwardly sigh, true to the style of the Joyful Union Sect.

But this was someone else’s family affair; as long as it didn’t harm others, or forcefully take civilian girls, and was mutually consensual, it was no one else’s business in this life or the one before, aside from legal marriage.

Dong!

A distant bell tolled, and suddenly a fragrance of medicine wafted through the air.

Gu Wen looked up towards the Qianfeng Tower outside the alley, a hint of killing intent causing Hee Huan’s expression to change slightly; for a fleeting moment, it seemed as if he saw the majestic head of a crimson dragon.

“The Pills are ready.”

His voice was even, with a subtle killing aura permeating.

Seeing Gu Wen’s stance, Hee Huan knew that a fierce battle was likely ahead and reminded, “Fellow Red Dust, be careful.

The individuals from the Major Sects who walk in the world always have two protectors accompanying them.

They’re not someone I, alone and unaided, can compare with.”

“Who is her Guardian?” Gu Wen asked.

“You do not know, Fellow Red Dust?” Hee Huan was somewhat surprised.

Gu Wen shook his head in response, “Many years of secluded cultivation have left me oblivious to the world, unaware of who is a hero.”

“In that case, Fellow Daoist’s expenses for coming here must not be small.”

Hee Huan was not suspicious, as there was nothing about it that called for doubt.

He replied, “Not everyone is qualified or has sufficient resources to activate a Breaking Realm Array.

Therefore, some geniuses choose to become the guardian for the successors of Major Sects.

The Fox Fairy’s guardian is also a well-known powerful figure, the twenty-first-ranked Ghost Lady, Yang Shanyu.”

“The Way of Ghosts and Spirits, mastering the spectral world, is not to be underestimated.”

Seeing Gu Wen not overly concerned, and in order to secure the Condensing Dao Pill for himself, Hee Huan added, “Fellow Daoist, the current ranking of the people’s list is not set.

Those with lower ranks are not necessarily weak, and those with higher ranks are not necessarily the strongest.”

Gu Wen nodded, staying alert.

But with the arrow nocked, he had no choice but to shoot; he had to seize every opportunity to gather resources.

The Spiritual Medicine he could obtain with silver and influence had reached its limit.

Daqian’s fate was unknown for how long it could last, akin to the saying: “better committing robbery than leading a mundane life.” If the chance arose, why not raid the Taisi Mansion?

Today was just a modest show of swordsmanship, a test of his abilities.

If he was still weak, he would continue to lie low; if he was unrivaled, he would sweep across Bianjing.

One last question, “Are all protectors great powers?”

“At the very least, they are all strong practitioners of the Refining God Returning Void Realm.”

The Mystical Sect’s cultivation had four major realms: Refining Essence and Transforming Qi, Qi Refinement, Refining God Returning to Void, and Harmonization.

The protectors were at least powerful practitioners of the Seventh Level.

“How powerful are they?”

“Due to the limits of fate, very few survive beyond it.

Those exceeding it will have their lives shortened.

But Refining God Returning Void Realm practitioners are much stronger than me.”

“That’s enough.”

Gu Wen smiled lightly, “In the Immortal Land, one does not assess by realm but by talent.

If my talents surpass even the heavens, why should I fear True Monarchs and Godly Immortals?”

Madness!

Sheer madness!

Among the world’s many proud geniuses, everyone is high-spirited and arrogant, but very few fail to take True Monarchs into consideration.

However, Hee Huan liked it, and he too smiled and said, “Fellow Daoist, go ahead, if something really happens, I have a backup to get you out.

Even if you can’t snatch the Pill, today I still owe you a favor.”

Gu Wen took a step forward, emerging from the shadows.

His appearance instantly attracted countless gazes; the imperial guards ran toward him.

He did not hide, nor did he need to.

From ten paces away, he merely glanced, and the surrounding horses panicked and crashed chaotically, turning Dragon Bridge Street, once resplendent like brocade, into turmoil.

Several imperial guards, as if facing a formidable enemy, then began to step back, their blades trembling nonstop.

This is what it means to have great power within oneself!

The grandeur in his eyes was being shredded bit by bit; courtiers were trampled and wailed in the chaos of runaway carriages—things he had to grovel in front of in the past were now like sandcastles, crumbling as he passed.

And the violent machinery that sustained all this feared him.

Breathing heavily, Gu Wen could no longer suppress the smile at the corner of his mouth; he admitted he quite liked this scene.

Once he had the strength, he couldn’t help but trample this glorious Dragon Bridge, stomping on all these courtiers and officials.

“This Fellow Daoist, may I know your business at Qianfeng Tower?”

Yang Shanyu stood at the entrance with her beautiful posture, confronting the unwelcome Gu Wen.

As soon as she stepped out, she regretted it; a strong murderous intent locked on her, and her instincts transmitted a frantic warning.

Danger, the mysterious person in front of her was extremely dangerous!

“Bring me a furnace of Condensing Dao Pills.”

Gu Wen clenched his spear, its murderous aura exploding through the black cloth like fire and abyss; the dark red spear’s energy crawled over the spear’s body.

“Also, I’d like to ask for the guidance of rank twenty-one on the Man Ranking, and rank five of the Land Ranking, Fox Fairy.”

Boom!

The flagstones of Dragon Bridge Road shattered, and a glint of cold light wrapped in a soaring murderous glow came whistling toward them.

Yang Shanyu was prepared; her beautiful eyes shone with a faint light, her face turned pale in an instant, and her palm radiated a ghostly light far stronger than any fine steel.

Thump!

Spear clashed against palm, sending sparks flying.

Yang Shanyu attempted to grasp the spear’s head, clenching her palm, but in less than half a breath, her tiger’s mouth split, and blood seemed to be instantly sucked away by the spear’s head.

Untouchable!

Just as the thought arose, she retreated; a sky full of spear energies enveloped her, while a crimson dragon swooped down in an instant, shattering her spirits.

Unstoppable and inescapable!

Conquer the square inch, take no life within six feet.

It was just one spear thrust, as if to penetrate Yang Shanyu.

Sigh~

A gust of wind lifted her hair as her fingertip lightly tapped her forehead.

Yang Shanyu collapsed to the ground with a thud, looking up at the man in front of her—like an abyss, like a demon—with a pair of eyes exuding a calm murderous intent.

“You lost.”

“May I ask for your esteemed name, Brother?”

“A mere Loose Cultivator from the Red Dust.”

Gu Wen, spear in hand, stepped into Qianfeng Tower.

He saw an official hiding under a table and, not minding the trouble, approached him with a spear that punctured the man’s considerably plump body.

He then saw someone nearby, a fourth grade imperial official, and casually killed him too.

Noble scions, high-ranking ministers, distinguished elites—this place was indeed teeming with the elite.

Just by stretching out his hand, the spear broke skin and flesh like piercing through paper mache.

Blood-stained spear, like an abyss, like a demon.

Cultivation is indeed a beautiful thing!

“What a fine spear of the Way of Killing, I wonder whose disciple he is.”

An elderly voice came through, and before him, an aged woman appeared, stooped and walking with a cane, like a candle flickering in the wind.

“Young man, leave Qianfeng Tower now, and I’ll spare you…”

Before her words ended, Gu Wen’s figure flashed; the Moonset Step’s Second Level allowed him to instantly leap three meters, drawing within six feet.

The Qianfeng protector’s pupils dilated, and with all the Daoist Skill impossible to employ and the world losing its color, she saw only a red light.

Gu Wen, with all his might, thrust his spear out; the spear’s energy trailed like a tail for three meters, and the wind howled.

Boom!

The Qianfeng protector was thrown like a cannonball, countless chairs entangled with her, embedding into the wall, ultimately bringing the wall down with her.

She collapsed to the ground, bloody froth at her mouth, eyes full of disbelief.

“The Way of the Spear reaching the Divine…”

Dao Equaling the Heavens

54: Chapter 46 Red Dragon dharma form

54 -46 Red Dragon dharma form

The once luxurious venue was in shambles, with attendants dizzy on the ground, servants climbing out windows, and outside were the Imperial Guards glancing around, even the death-defying spectators were peeking from a distance.

Protector Qianfeng struggled to her feet, her spirit light dissipating from her body, and within a few breaths, her injuries had healed, releasing an aura many times stronger than before.

Mana inflated like a balloon, expanding a hundredfold in an instant.

Before Gu Wen could react, a faint hum sounded mysteriously in the void, and the world pulsated with an odd ripple.

It seemed as if in the void countless needles existed, and once the aura expanded to a certain point, it would burst, causing Protector Qianfeng’s aura to weaken, her face pale, yet her body fully recovered.

Was this the so-called fate of Immortal Land?

It was Gu Wen’s first time witnessing such a bizarre scene, when any power exerted beyond a certain threshold was suppressed.

Judging by her complexion, this suppression seemed harmful; her body unharmed but her essence severely diminished.

Protector Qianfeng offered no explanations, her spirit light continuing to dissipate, and Gu Wen didn’t inquire.

In life-and-death combat, one must stabilize their energy in their core, as victory or defeat often hinged on a moment.

Suddenly, a crisp voice rang out.

“Protector, you should step back.

The pills of the Zhao family’s ninth son are not worth your life.”

“Yes, Miss.”

Protector Qianfeng with a bowed back slowly left, assisted by Yang Shanyu, as both exited the stage.

Gu Wen didn’t try to stop them; instead, he turned and headed up the stairs, straight to the sixth floor.

Robbery must be quick; killing was secondary.

As Gu Wen reached the fifth floor, he again smelled that faint fragrance, the bell-like voice sounding once more.

“Fellow Daoist, is such a furious demeanor just for a batch of pills?”

Her voice, as always, was soft and enticing, carrying a power that scratched at one’s mind.

The air was filled with perfume with certain medicinal properties, even the reflections from behind the curtains of the doors seemed profound.

“Being a monk, I seek wealth but do not harm lives.

Fellow Daoist, would you fight to the death for the pills of the Zhao family’s ninth son?”

Gu Wen retorted, then cleared his mind with his jade sword, step by step he moved towards the sixth floor, the voice in his ears never ceasing, the images in his mind being slashed again and again.

Though harmless to him, it was pervasive, seemingly endless.

Familiar thoughts arose, as if seeing a beauty in a past life, deciding on a child’s name, the simplest yet most treacherous seduction.

Gain favor first, then lead their thoughts.

When the heart lingers, it moves inevitably.

“Entrusted by others, naturally I must fulfill my duty completely.

Moreover, Fellow Daoist, how do you warrant me conceding immediately upon arrival?”

Lu Chan’s voice turned slightly cold, the dimly lit corridor blooming with spirit light.

An array?

Gu Wen glanced briefly, his body shooting forward like a cannonball.

A golden light emerged, his body heavy as if weighed down, crushing the floor as he stepped.

The corridor’s curtains suddenly moved as if alive, twisting into thick needle-like tendrils that thrust violently toward him.

His long spear swept across, the curtain swallowed by the spear’s aura, feeling no resistance as if striking nothing.

An illusion technique?

More needle-like tendrils attacked, the corridor around him expanding, one meter, two meters, three meters…

up to ten meters.

He seemed to be standing on Dragon Bridge Avenue, curtains continuously falling from the Nine Heavens.
